  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_05430739-f9db-4394-bda5-039ee3fd4fc0'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }
  //]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer10652084735191227204"><div>
  <div>
    <p>John Wayne Cleaver is dangerous, and he knows it.<br/><br/>He's spent his life doing his best not to live up to his potential.<br/><br/>He's obsessed with serial killers, but really doesn't want to become one.   <span id="freeText10652084735191227204" style="display:none"><div>
  <div>
    <p>John Wayne Cleaver is dangerous, and he knows it.<br /><br />He's spent his life doing his best not to live up to his potential.<br /><br />He's obsessed with serial killers, but really doesn't want to become one. So for his own sake, and the safety of those around him, he lives by rigid rules he's written for himself, practicing normal life as if it were a private religion that could save him from damnation.<br /><br />Dead bodies are normal to John. He likes them, actually. They don't demand or expect the empathy he's unable to offer. Perhaps that's what gives him the objectivity to recognize that there's something different about the body the police have just found behind the Wash-n-Dry Laundromat---and to appreciate what that difference means.<br /><br />Now, for the first time, John has to confront a danger outside himself, a threat he can't control, a menace to everything and everyone he would love, if only he could.<br /><br />Dan Wells' debut novel is the first volume of a trilogy that will keep you awake and then haunt your dreams.</p>
  </div>
</div></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2140333214" />

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2140333214?book_show_action=true">Oct 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=absolute-favorites">absolute-favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140333214" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3207542157875237314"><blockquote> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585499756i/29193446._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><b>Stuck at home?</b> Got some time on your hands? Want to start <b>a long series</b>? But you don't want a dud?<br/><br/>Check out this<b>
  <u> <a href='https://youtu.be/Xxa4N5jdFa8' rel='nofollow noopener'>booktube video</a></u>
</b> all about which series are worth your time (and which ones aren't)! <br/><br/><b>
  <u>Here's the Written Review!</u>
</b><br/><br/><b> What if a serial killer...doesn't <i>want</i> to become a murderer?</b><br/><br/>John Wayne Cleaver knows he has all the hallmarks of a serial killer.<br/><br/>He likes to stalk people, hurt animals and fantasizes about killing friends and family. <blockquote>
  <i> Fear is a ... it's a weird thing, when you thi</i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText3207542157875237314" style="display:none"><blockquote> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585499756i/29193446._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>Stuck at home?</b> Got some time on your hands? Want to start <b>a long series</b>? But you don't want a dud?<br><br>Check out this<b>
  <u> <a href="https://youtu.be/Xxa4N5jdFa8" rel="nofollow noopener">booktube video</a></u>
</b> all about which series are worth your time (and which ones aren't)! <br><br><b>
  <u>Here's the Written Review!</u>
</b><br><br><b> What if a serial killer...doesn't <i>want</i> to become a murderer?</b><br><br>John Wayne Cleaver knows he has all the hallmarks of a serial killer.<br><br>He likes to stalk people, hurt animals and fantasizes about killing friends and family. <blockquote>
  <i> Fear is a ... it's a weird thing, when you think about it. People are only afraid of other things, they're never afraid of themselves. </i>
</blockquote><b>John is afraid of himself</b> - or at least he's afraid of what he could become. <br><br>So, he's created a set of rules avoid any situation or thought that could encourage those traits.<br><br> If he notices himself following someone, he will not look at them for a week. If he wants to hurt someone, he has to say something nice. <br><br>He has rules to help him cope and manages quite well(ish) to <b>pass for a normal kid.</b><br><br>Yet, if another serial killer comes to town...what would be safer? <br><br>Following his rules or allowing himself to indulge his killer tendencies and hunt down a murderer? <br><br>And to top it all, there's a cute girl at school and <b>his mom is trying to hook them up</b>. He doesn't know what's worse, that it's <i>his mom</i> whose facilitating this girl's interaction with a potential serial killer or the fact that he likes her back.<br><br>There is a fabulous twist that brings the term "serial killer" into a whole new light.<br><br>I love how John is doing his absolute best to curb <b>all killer-instincts</b> AND he has a great family to support him. <br><br>This is a crazy-good mixture of familial love and homicidal urges wrapped up in one book.<br><br>One of my favorites! <br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>

<div id="review_97978137" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/97978137" />
    <a title="Stephen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen"><img alt="Stephen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1311616811p2/1413439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/97978137?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen" href="/user/show/1413439-stephen">Stephen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=psychos">psychos</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=hardboiled-and-noir">hardboiled-and-noir</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=2006-2010">2006-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1413439-stephen?shelf=angels-demons-heaven-hell">angels-demons-heaven-hell</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer97978137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer801646919571994077">My reaction when a third of the way through the book <b>“IT”</b> happened was something like…<br/><a href='http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Decorated%20images/?action=view&current=surprised-black-spider-monkey-funny.jpg' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333886i/693502.jpg' alt='Photobucket' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>For those of you that have read the book, you know EXACTLY what I am talking about. For everyone else, let me explain as best I can without any spoilers. <br/><br/>Our story begins in a small town with a wonderful introduction to John Wayne Cleaver. John is 15 years old boy who is obsessed with serial killers. This obsession is the result of he himself having many of the traits and characteristics of a serial killer </span>
  <span id="freeText801646919571994077" style="display:none">My reaction when a third of the way through the book <b>“IT”</b> happened was something like…<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Decorated%20images/?action=view&amp;current=surprised-black-spider-monkey-funny.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333886i/693502.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For those of you that have read the book, you know EXACTLY what I am talking about. For everyone else, let me explain as best I can without any spoilers. <br><br>Our story begins in a small town with a wonderful introduction to John Wayne Cleaver. John is 15 years old boy who is obsessed with serial killers. This obsession is the result of he himself having many of the traits and characteristics of a serial killer and struggling desperately against his inner “urges.” John has decided that by learning how these people act and what drives them, he can determine what actions to avoid in order to keep from killing anyone...Sounds pretty sensible to me, but then again I've never killed anyone....well, except for food and that doesn't count.<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Gifs/?action=view&amp;current=farvabeans-1.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380333886ra/693503.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Uh...sorry about that, just kidding..heh...heh...Anyway, to help John in his quest not to commit heinous butchery, he has developed strict rules that he follows in order to try and be (or at least appear) normal. For example, if someone makes John angry he will compliment them. If he finds himself observing someone, even unintentionally, he will make himself avoid that person for one week to avoid “stalking” them. These were very interesting and this part of the book was excellent. <br><br>Now, for those of you that read or watch Dexter, comparisons to that series are both accurate and appropriate. Apart from their age, the only significant difference between the characters is that John has not yet killed. Apart from that the similarities are certainly there. They both have “routines” they follow to be normal. They both “work” around dead bodies (Dexter is a blood-splatter analyst while John’s family are the local morticians) and they both struggle with “their inner monster.” Regardless, I was absolutely loving the book as John (like Dexter) is a fascinating character and the descriptions of his daily routines and his struggle against his inner monster were very well done. <br><br>In addition to learning about John, the central plot of the book involves the discovery that an actual serial killer is on the loose in John’s small town. It seems that some madman is killing older men and stealing parts of their body. Of course, John is fascinated and begins trying to figure out who the killer is and how he is selecting his victims. <br>...<br>...<br>Okay, let's just pause and take a moment to appreciate how we got to this point because the road is gonna get pretty rough ahead.<br>.<br>.<br>.<br>Ready to continue....Okay, so up to this point, everything about the book was excellent. As I finished the first 100 pages my rating was sitting in high 4 star and maybe even 5 star territory and I was just as happy as I could be....AND THEN...ON PAGE 121...EVERYTHING CHANGED....BECAUSE....<b>IT HAPPENED</b>…and the book completely:<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Decorated%20images/?action=view&amp;current=125_125_edited-2.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333886i/693504.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>This was a complete FULL STOP,WTF just happened moment for me that left me stunned and bewildered. It was like the “infamous” end of the movie <i>The Crying Game</i>, except that while that was shocking and excellent...this was just shocking and painful. Very, very painful...<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Gifs/?action=view&amp;current=OUCH.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380333886ra/693505.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>Well, neither I nor the book ever really recovered from <b>IT</b>. <b>IT</b> kinda took the wind out of my sails. Now the rest of the book was not horrible and there were some interesting portions in the rest of the book. Unfortunately, after <b>IT</b> I was basically disengaged from the narrative. I just felt….empty…<br><a href="http://s153.photobucket.com/albums/s207/sullypython/Goodreads/?action=view&amp;current=gaping10.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333886i/693506.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So, overall the book was good but it could have been great if <b>IT</b> had not happened. Unfortunately, <b>IT</b> did happen and when <b>IT</b> happened, <b>IT</b> kinda ruined it for me…Oh well shIT happens!!!<br><br>P.S. For those of you who have requested to know what <b>IT</b> is, here you go...<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The serial killer loose in the town turns out to be a DEMON which comes completely out of left field since the book was reading like a straight YA crime thriller <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="801646919571994077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2255216332?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook " href="/book/show/15998401-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=thriller-suspense">thriller-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=audio">audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=mature-ya">mature-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2255216332" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1571323863983604138">Alright. I really didn't quite know what I was getting into with this book.<br/>I <i>thought</i> it was some sort of a YA mystery/thriller with a young sociopath as the main character. And, yes. It <i>is</i> that.<br/>But it's also a paranormal story with real demons in it.<br/>So...yeah. I think that's something you should probably know upfront.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570987432ra/28288420.gif' width='400' height='230' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Ok, so the gist is that this kid named John, who is trying his dead-level best <i>not</i> to turn into a serial killer, ends up becoming the only one who can save his town from potentially</span>
  <span id="freeText1571323863983604138" style="display:none">Alright. I really didn't quite know what I was getting into with this book.<br>I <i>thought</i> it was some sort of a YA mystery/thriller with a young sociopath as the main character. And, yes. It <i>is</i> that.<br>But it's also a paranormal story with real demons in it.<br>So...yeah. I think that's something you should probably know upfront.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570987432ra/28288420.gif" width="400" height="230" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Ok, so the gist is that this kid named John, who is trying his dead-level best <i>not</i> to turn into a serial killer, ends up becoming the only one who can save his town from potentially the <i>most sympathetic</i> murdering demon I've ever read about.<br><i>Or listened to, since this was an audiobook that I downloaded on the fly because it was 'currently available' from my library and I needed something quick - which explains why I didn't realize it had all the spooky monster shit in advance.</i><br>Anyway, the point <i>is</i>, John's sleepy small town is being rocked by a vicious killer and everyone is in a tizzy.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1570987432ra/28288421.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Spoilery things happen, people die, &amp; John has to deal with a real demon <i>and</i> his inner demon before the story is over. I enjoyed the dark humor and thought the narrator (John Allen Nelson) did a fantastic job of bringing the whole thing to life.<br>I can see there are quite a few books in this series, but I feel as though if I wanted to stop here, I could. I'm not sure yet, to be honest. <br>We'll see.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_137727289" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/137727289" />
    <a title="Flannery" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/652877-flannery"><img alt="Flannery" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312843258p2/652877.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/137727289?book_show_action=true">Jan 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flannery" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flannery" href="/user/show/652877-flannery">Flannery</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Flannery by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/4626387-linda">Linda</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=kcls">kcls</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=read-in-2011">read-in-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=reviewed-2011">reviewed-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/652877-flannery?shelf=young-adult-teen">young-adult-teen</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer137727289" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5871403603703816220">John Wayne Cleaver lives in a mortuary. But before you go thinking this is all fun and games like <a href='http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0102492/' rel='nofollow noopener'>My Girl</a> (well, at least before Thomas J and the bees), you should know that John Wayne is a killer. Well, at least he thinks he is. As a teenager, his internal monster makes life considerably harder, especially because John feels no connection to his peers and little to no emotion. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7617119.I_Am_Not_A_Serial_Killer__John_Cleaver___1_' title='I Am Not A Serial Killer (John Cleaver, #1) by Dan Wells' rel='nofollow noopener'>I Am Not A Serial Killer</a> follows John as he deals with having a serial killer in his town--Will being so close to an ac</span>
  <span id="freeText5871403603703816220" style="display:none">John Wayne Cleaver lives in a mortuary. But before you go thinking this is all fun and games like <a href="http://www.imdb.com/title/tt0102492/" rel="nofollow noopener">My Girl</a> (well, at least before Thomas J and the bees), you should know that John Wayne is a killer. Well, at least he thinks he is. As a teenager, his internal monster makes life considerably harder, especially because John feels no connection to his peers and little to no emotion. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7617119.I_Am_Not_A_Serial_Killer__John_Cleaver___1_" title="I Am Not A Serial Killer (John Cleaver, #1) by Dan Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">I Am Not A Serial Killer</a> follows John as he deals with having a serial killer in his town--Will being so close to an actual killer cause John to lose control of his own monster? <br /><br />At times, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2740668.Dan_Wells" title="Dan Wells" rel="nofollow noopener">Dan Wells</a>' debut novel seems a bit too juvenile. Anyone who knows my reading habits knows how much young adult literature I read. My expectations of this work were that I was going to be reading Dexter Lite. In actuality, this book had very little gore and it read like someone did research on serial killers, found out about the <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Macdonald_triad" rel="nofollow noopener">Macdonald Triad</a> and then just wrote a book about it. I don't meant that to sound harsh but I honestly feel that it could've been so much better. John is in high school but it felt like a middle reader book. (as much as a book about serial killers can)<br /><br />In terms of the storyline, I was trucking along until page 103, when a total WTF moment pops up. Without spoilers, I'll just say that I thought I was reading a book about a serial killer in reality. Turns out, I was reading a book with a supernatural/paranormal element. Major buzzkill. There were just too many "no way" type moments for me in this story--the one that kept popping up (much to my dismay) was the fact that John simultaneously shovels snow several times a week yet also bikes everywhere (even to a lake outside town). If there is enough snow to be shoveling more than once a week, you are not bicycling. Especially in a small town where there is less traffic to melt the snow on the roads. (Yes, I know it is possible and some people enjoy biking in winter but I don't buy it here) [note: More "no way" moments below but with spoilers]<br /><br />There are tons of glowing reviews for this book on Goodreads, so maybe it is just me. And that's great. But this book is the first in a series of three--I will definitely not be reading any further. I see that a few of my friends on here gave up on this one and to them I say--Cheers on a choice well made:-) <br /><br />And to Linda, whom I still trust for recommendations, I was excited to read this one. You were right to recommend it. But I need more blood and guts in my killer novels! <br /><br /><br />****************SPOILER ALERT************<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Also, and this is a huge also, if a freaking demon has been killing people for decades, I'm pretty sure he'd catch on to a high school kid who keeps leaving notes for him. Someone that is used to stalking prey will not just go on with every day life (la-la-la) while someone is trying to expose them. Are you kidding me? They'd spy back and figure out who it is. <br /><br />A large part of me thinks the paranormal element might've been added in because the book is YA and, for some reason, either the publisher or the author felt like it would be too gruesome to have a regular human doing all the killing and body part snatching. To them, I say, yeah right. Have you read YA these days? Bring on the regular serial killers!<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5871403603703816220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_103682601" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/103682601" />
    <a title="Kemper" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/405390-kemper"><img alt="Kemper" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1495476851p2/405390.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103682601?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kemper" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kemper" href="/user/show/405390-kemper">Kemper</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=serial-killers">serial-killers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=crime-mystery">crime-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/405390-kemper?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103682601" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8866219561083353537">Ever since Hannibal Lector flirted with Clarice Starling by telling her about his favorite recipes, it seems like every other thriller features some kind of deranged but brilliant serial killer. It’s gotten beyond boring, but occasionally some writer will manage to come up with a fresh perspective on the genre. Jeff Lindsay’s Dexter series put a unique twist on the notion of the serial killer. (Or at least he did until he wrote the utterly crappy <i>Dexter in the Dark</i>.) Now Dan Wells is taking a ne</span>
  <span id="freeText8866219561083353537" style="display:none">Ever since Hannibal Lector flirted with Clarice Starling by telling her about his favorite recipes, it seems like every other thriller features some kind of deranged but brilliant serial killer. It’s gotten beyond boring, but occasionally some writer will manage to come up with a fresh perspective on the genre. Jeff Lindsay’s Dexter series put a unique twist on the notion of the serial killer. (Or at least he did until he wrote the utterly crappy <i>Dexter in the Dark</i>.) Now Dan Wells is taking a new approach to the concept.<br /><br />John Wayne Cleaver is a teen-age boy who lives with his mother at the funeral home she runs with her twin sister. John has had a history of bed wetting, killing small animals and starting fires, and he’s very fond of helping prepare the dead bodies for funerals. He’s also obsessed with serial killers, and his reading about them has made him realize that he’s already showing all the classic signs of becoming one.<br /><br />John sets strict rules for himself to keep from becoming a killer, but he’s still considered an outcast and a freak by his classmates. He also has to see a therapist who he tells about his efforts to not engage in mass murder. However, when a string of grisly murders occur that terrify the town, John can barely contain his excitement that a serial killer is operating nearby. However, John will find out that this killer is worse than even his deranged mind can imagine.<br /><br />The first third of his book had me completely intrigued. I loved the notion of someone fighting against their own inclinations. John has so fully accepted the idea that he is a serial killer, that he never stops to question why he’d work so hard to avoid becoming one if he truly is a sociopath. <br /><br />However, the book takes a wild turn that I didn't really enjoy. Plus, I could never get entirely over the similarities to the Dexter series. <br /><br />It’s a quick read and the first in a planned trilogy. It was good enough I’ll check out the second volume, but I was far more interested in John’s psychology than the plot.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8866219561083353537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/147580267" />
    <a title="Stacy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4852567-stacy"><img alt="Stacy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1528737509p2/4852567.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/147580267?book_show_action=true">Feb 11, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacy" href="/user/show/4852567-stacy">Stacy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">`</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4852567-stacy?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4852567-stacy?shelf=couldnt-finish">couldnt-finish</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer147580267" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12223190927317566813">I wanted to read this book because of my fascination with serial killers and the intriguing slant in the main character's relationship with himself.<br/>While reading, I was put off by Wells' writing style. It came off as juvenile in that he writes as though he doesn't trust his readers to figure out fairly obvious things for themselves. He posts many unnecessary/rhetorical questions that the reader is (hopefully, or rather should be) already wondering about on her own. It's muddled in redundancy.<br/>All</span>
  <span id="freeText12223190927317566813" style="display:none">I wanted to read this book because of my fascination with serial killers and the intriguing slant in the main character's relationship with himself.<br />While reading, I was put off by Wells' writing style. It came off as juvenile in that he writes as though he doesn't trust his readers to figure out fairly obvious things for themselves. He posts many unnecessary/rhetorical questions that the reader is (hopefully, or rather should be) already wondering about on her own. It's muddled in redundancy.<br />All of this I could have put aside, and tried to, for the sake of the still intriguing concept and somewhat likable main character. However, a few more than 100 pages in, it took an unforgivable turn for the worse. I don't want to spoil anything for those who haven't read it yet and may still want to, so I will spare you any sort of real detail. Suffice it to say that it became very obvious fairly quickly that this book wasn't one I would care for in the slightest. I put it down without finishing it, which is something I usually have a hard time doing, but it was fairly easy with this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12223190927317566813" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_104099906" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/104099906" />
    <a title="Jason Brown (Toastx2)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1541278-jason-brown-toastx2"><img alt="Jason Brown (Toastx2)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588096994p2/1541278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/104099906?book_show_action=true">May 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason Brown (Toastx2)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason Brown (Toastx2)" href="/user/show/1541278-jason-brown-toastx2">Jason Brown (Toastx2)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1541278-jason-brown-toastx2?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer104099906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14220033225736158718">I think my wife is a serial killer waiting to be unleashed on the world.<br/><br/>I had not heard of this novel but ran across a Powell’s Books author reading late last month by Dan Wells. I read a summary of his recent book and then scheduled appropriately to go and listen to him. Jenn went with me and whispered creepy serial killer/mass murderer stats in my ear.. it was disturbing how much she knew.. When Dan asked people to name 5 killers in order to win a t-shirt, she stayed quiet and named 14 under h</span>
  <span id="freeText14220033225736158718" style="display:none">I think my wife is a serial killer waiting to be unleashed on the world.<br /><br />I had not heard of this novel but ran across a Powell’s Books author reading late last month by Dan Wells. I read a summary of his recent book and then scheduled appropriately to go and listen to him. Jenn went with me and whispered creepy serial killer/mass murderer stats in my ear.. it was disturbing how much she knew.. When Dan asked people to name 5 killers in order to win a t-shirt, she stayed quiet and named 14 under her breath. no one but the Author could compete with her, naming less than five, 2 of which Wells had used as examples……<br /><br />please send the police after her FIRST if i ever drop off the radar (after she reads this, my stats will weigh against me.).. DO NOT enter our home, make sure to arrive with witnesses, and be careful if she offers you refreshments, it is a distraction tactic. Bring gelato if you plan on surviving..<br /><br />so, the long –&gt; short of it is that i bought a copy of I AM NOT A SERIAL KILLER. Dan Wells scribbled his John Hancock into the cover and i went home.. I had some must reads already waiting that needed to be pushed through my brain machine before i could get to this.. How i waited nearly a month, i really do not know….. it was very, very good…<br /><br />John Wayne Cleaver is a 15 year old boy in a small town. Overall he is a nice kid who just can’t find any connection to the people around him. he has only one friend and is a freak among his peers. He grew up in a family of morticians. He helps out around the house and business. John is an outcast because he firmly believes he will grow up to be a serial killer.<br /><br />John does not WANT to be a serial killer, but he thinks that the universe has stacked the deck against him, starting with his name. His namesake is an actor who shares a name with a killer (c’mon pilgrim..). His father is Sam Cleaver, making him the Son of Sam. His last name is a tool for cutting meat.<br /><br />Interestingly enough, the town John lives in has a new killer hanging around, killing people and leaving their bodies lying about with parts missing. John obsessively investigates the killer, attempting to determine his motives and methodologies. This is in part because of his interest in the subject matter, and in part because of his fear of joining the ranks.. the more he knows, the better prepared he will be.<br /><br />This really was a great book. IANASK is a mild thriller, and a must read for anyone who has found themselves spending an afternoon reading through the Internet Crime Library or whiling away nights watching true crime shows on TV. Wells did a great job breaking down the mind of a killer and really leaves you mentally cheering for the 15 year old sociopath that is the main character. You know he could turn out to be a horrible person in a couple years, but hope for the best because really, his is just a great kid. classically misunderstood.<br /><br />The book is portioned well, focusing on John’s internal struggle as much as his obsessions with finding and stopping the local killer.<br /><br />It is a little gory in some spots, but not overly so.. of course, i could also be desensitized :).. ok, well, just assume that i am desensitized..<br /><br />One of my favorite aspects of John Cleaver is that he has already identified character traits of his that make him fear for his future. He has created a series of rules that will help himself suppress these character traits. These rules are mandatory to keep himself from crossing over, they keep his darker side in check.. ignoring these rules and he threatens to unleash his darkness, self named “Mr. Monster”<br />Examples of his rules:<br />- To keep stalker qualities subdued, he avoids people for a full week if he finds he is taking too much interest in them. too many conversations and he cuts off contact. if he finds himself following them home, they get back burner’d.<br /><br />- If he feels like doing bodily harm on someone, he should distract himself by being overly nice and saying nice things about them. Thinking and saying nice tings tends to push back the bad… you know the classic “Think Positive” motivational posters? He should have one tattooed on the back of his hand.<br /><br />- He must hand out with Max, another outcast in his grade. having max as a friend makes him more normal. after all, sociopaths do not have friends, so having a friend combats his sociopathy.<br /><br />The book is humorous and intense in all the right places.<br />If you pick this book up, let me know what you thought of the Halloween Dance chapter. It cracked me up enough that i read sections aloud to people who were uncomfortable with a large insistent bearded man enthusiastically reading aloud a book titled ‘I am not a serial killer’… don’t get why that would make people feel “off” but it apparently does :)<br /><br />surprised that i still have a job considering the number of people who gave me uncomfortable looks on the elevator or in the break room.<br /><br />This was book one in a trilogy, i am very interested to see how the characters in this series turn out. Mr Wells, Get to releasing the books.. NOW! if you need someone to read them in advance, i would gladly volunteer :) (hint hint)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14220033225736158718" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1323444331" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1323444331" />
    <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please"><img alt="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1570038444p2/8422853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1323444331?book_show_action=true">Jul 02, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ " href="/user/show/8422853-chelsea-peril-please">Chelsea ❤Peril Please❤ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=male-pov">male-pov</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=my-favorite-covers">my-favorite-covers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8422853-chelsea-peril-please?shelf=could-read-over-and-over-again">could-read-over-and-over-again</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1323444331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2564808424972225426"><br/><blockquote>
  <b><i>You are evil</i>, said myself. <i>You are Mr. Monster. You are nothing. You are me.</i></b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Well well well...what an odd slice of fun this was. Simplistic and understated, this book really doesn't try to be anything other than what it says it is, making for not only a fun, easy read, but a very touching one, as well. It's not easy to read about a diagnosed sociopath...well, at least not for the average person. For me? It felt more <b>authentic and real</b>. I became entwined and engrossed with this character in th</span>
  <span id="freeText2564808424972225426" style="display:none"><br><blockquote>
  <b><i>You are evil</i>, said myself. <i>You are Mr. Monster. You are nothing. You are me.</i></b>
</blockquote><br><br>Well well well...what an odd slice of fun this was. Simplistic and understated, this book really doesn't try to be anything other than what it says it is, making for not only a fun, easy read, but a very touching one, as well. It's not easy to read about a diagnosed sociopath...well, at least not for the average person. For me? It felt more <b>authentic and real</b>. I became entwined and engrossed with this character in the early stages of the book, making it enjoyable from page one all the way until the end. And then there's that damn middle part that just...ugh...it was so...ah, fuck it-<b>It made me laugh. Hard.</b><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"So you have coincidental links to two serial killers," he said. "That's a little odd, I admit, but I'm still not seeing a cosmic conspiracy against you."<br>"My last name is 'Cleaver,'" I said. "How many people do you know who are named after two serial killers and a murder weapon?"</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>I mean seriously?? He really went there? You've got to be kidding me. And yet....is it odd that, in the end, I kind of <i>loved</i> where this went??? I can now see why some people didn't like the direction this novel took, but I actually, after my initial shock, LOVED IT! It took a bit, I'll admit, to get past the <b>absurdity with which this was presented</b>. But let me ask you this: For me, being the type of reader that I am, why <i>wouldn't</i> I love the fact that this <s>little</s> twist made it all the more perilous? Yeah, it was totally unbelievable. Yeah, it was an odd direction to go. And, yes, it will not be for everyone. But, for whatever reason, I decided I really liked it-<b>Logic be damned.</b><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>I think that fire is more alive than we are-brighter, hotter, more sure of itself and where it wants to go. Fire doesn't settle; fire doesn't tolerate; fire doesn't "get by." Fire <i>does</i>.<br>Fire <i>is</i>.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>I really did have an internal struggle on whether or not I liked what was happening in this one. I wrestled with the idea that, while I am in love with these types of books, this was really dumb. But it comes down to more than that, it comes down to <b>if the positive outweighs the negative</b>...and, for me, it did. And that big positive that made this whole book worth it? Our main character, John.<br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>People scurry around, doing their little jobs and raising their little families and shouting their meaningless emotions to the world, and all the while you just watch from the sidelines, bewildered. This drives some sociopaths to feel superior, as if the whole of humanity were simply animals to be hunted or put down; others feel a hot, jealous rage, desperate to have what they cannot. I simply felt alone, one leaf sitting miles away from a giant, communal pile.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br><b>Emotionless</b>, <b>lacking empathy</b>, and <b>a social outcast</b>, John was my favorite type of character, at the moment. Well, I like a little more empathy in my boys, but, hey-You get what I mean. Not without the quirky inner monologue or the twisted humor of the writing would this book have succeeded-of that I'm sure. John would not be a likable character to read about had we not gotten his odd rationalizations of the goings on around him or the way he views human flaws, such as love and loyalty. In a way, <b>he's broken</b>. He longs to feel something, <i>anything</i>, if only to be like those around him-<b>He can't even cry</b>. He gets jealous that others have this ability, and that's why he is so fascinated with serial killers-weird sounding, I know! But, when you feel like you're on the verge of being one yourself, it only makes sense to latch onto the one connection in this world you are sure is your only link to humanity. <br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"You're weird, man," said Max, taking another bite of his sandwich. "That's all there is to say. Someday you're going to kill a whole bunch of people-probably more than ten, because you're such an overachiever-and then they're going to have me on TV and ask if I saw this coming, and I'm going to say,'Hell yes, that guy was seriously screwed up.'"<br>"Then I guess I have to kill you first," I said.</b>
</blockquote><br><br><br>You heard me right-<b>He thinks he is destined to be a serial killer</b>. And, because of this, he has a set of rules he rigidly follows. And it has worked...until a serial killer comes to town. Every day his 'monster' threatens to leak out, to identify with this new murderer-sorry, sorry, not murderer...SERIAL KILLER-in town. But when he finds out who is killing, he takes responsibility into his own hands. <b>Who better to find a serial killer</b>...than a destined-to-be serial killer?<br><br><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>"I've been clinically diagnosed with sociopathy," I said. "Do you know what that means?"<br>"It means you're a freak," he said.<br>"It means that you're about as important to me as a cardboard box," I said. "You're just a thing-a piece of garbage that no one's thrown away yet. Is that what you want me to say?"<br>"Shut up," said Rob. He was still acting tough, but I could see his bluster was starting to fail-he didn't know what to say.<br>"The thing about boxes," I said, "is that you can open them up. Even though they're completely boring on the outside, there might be something interesting on the inside. So while you're saying all of these stupid, boring things, I'm imagining what it would be like to cut you open and see what you've got in there."</b>
</blockquote><br><br>-lol, is it deranged I laughed and loved that?<br><br><br>Stellar, spot-on writing, wicked humor, and absolutely gruesome scenes that make you think deeper about life in general....I really liked this book. And, after looking at book two ratings and reviews, it seems <b>book two is even darker, grittier, <i>better</i></b>. I cannot wait until I get the time to read book two. Because once John's exterior cracked? I fell in love with him. I can't wait to see how he wrestles with his dark side.<br><br><br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><a href="http://starcrossedbookblog.com/chelsea/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img height="200" width="320" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1491628712i/22430034._SX540_.jpg" alt="descriptive text here" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <u>
  <b></b>

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055977i/15660595.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1438055639i/15660580.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_2366508747" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2366508747" />
    <a title="Mort" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67602782-mort"><img alt="Mort" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586932919p2/67602782.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2366508747?book_show_action=true">Apr 19, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mort" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mort" href="/user/show/67602782-mort">Mort</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2366508747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9442626045770392774">Surprisingly good...<br/>With all the mixed reviews I've read, I wasn't expecting to enjoy it so much.<br/><br/>John Wayne Cleaver is a TEENAGER. A loner and freak. His mother and aunt owns a mortuary and he helps with the dead bodies when they arrive. His father has all but disappeared from his life.<br/>John Wayne Cleaver is a SOCIOPATH. He is obsessed with serial killers and knows exactly what he is, but he makes himself follow some self-imposed rules to keep from becoming a killer himself.<br/>John Wayne Cleaver is </span>
  <span id="freeText9442626045770392774" style="display:none">Surprisingly good...<br />With all the mixed reviews I've read, I wasn't expecting to enjoy it so much.<br /><br />John Wayne Cleaver is a TEENAGER. A loner and freak. His mother and aunt owns a mortuary and he helps with the dead bodies when they arrive. His father has all but disappeared from his life.<br />John Wayne Cleaver is a SOCIOPATH. He is obsessed with serial killers and knows exactly what he is, but he makes himself follow some self-imposed rules to keep from becoming a killer himself.<br />John Wayne Cleaver is the only one who knows the serial killer in their town is actually a DEMON. Will he be able to stop it? More important, will he even want to?<br /><br />When I came across the term "YA", I really thought it would be too tame for my taste. But the author, whether knowingly or not, made this story deeper than what appears on the surface.<br />Yes, it is an entertaining story, but underneath it all some social issues are raised. You can decide for yourself whether you find it interesting or not, but I liked the fact that it made me think about some things there are seemingly no correct answers for:<br /><br />At what age does a child realize that they are not normal, unable to feel like everybody else?<br />Do they all pretend in order to fit in, but will they be forever the outsider looking in?<br />How much damage does a broken marriage do to a child, especially if one parent disappears as if writing off that child?<br />How essential in physical human contact, especially from a mother as a single parent?<br />Can a "demon" be more human than a "normal" person?<br />Whose side will you, the reader, pick in this story - the sociopath or the demon?<br /><br />Very glad I took the chance with this one.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9442626045770392774" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_3200177232" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3200177232" />
    <a title="Claude&#39;s Bookzone" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/87993607-claude-s-bookzone"><img alt="Claude&#39;s Bookzone" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1559447365p2/87993607.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3200177232?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claude&#39;s Bookzone" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claude&#39;s Bookzone" href="/user/show/87993607-claude-s-bookzone">Claude&#39;s Bookzone</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3200177232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1840023065666194686">I'm struggling between a 3.5 or 4 Stars. 4 Stars for the story but 3.5 for the actual writing etc. I'll go with a 3.75 rounded up to 4 Stars.<br/><br/>CW: Gruesome murder scenes, thoughts of killing, thoughts of animal cruelty, previous acts of animal cruelty, pyromania ( well he lights fires as a release instead of fulfilling his desire to kill), deaths of loved ones, described brutality, described preparation of bodies by mortician.<br/><br/>John is an expert on serial killers. He understands their motives, needs</span>
  <span id="freeText1840023065666194686" style="display:none">I'm struggling between a 3.5 or 4 Stars. 4 Stars for the story but 3.5 for the actual writing etc. I'll go with a 3.75 rounded up to 4 Stars.<br /><br />CW: Gruesome murder scenes, thoughts of killing, thoughts of animal cruelty, previous acts of animal cruelty, pyromania ( well he lights fires as a release instead of fulfilling his desire to kill), deaths of loved ones, described brutality, described preparation of bodies by mortician.<br /><br />John is an expert on serial killers. He understands their motives, needs and methods. Why? Because he has all the markers to become one himself. He has been diagnosed with conduct disorder.<br /><br /><u>Sociopathy 101</u><br />A conduct disorder is a mental disorder diagnosed in childhood or adolescence that basically means they display some quite anti-social behaviour. If the behaviour continues until after the age of 18 they may be diagnosed with 'anti-social personality disorder' which is sometimes called sociopathy. A sociopath is a manipulative person who basically doesn't care about other people's feelings or what is 'right' or 'wrong'. They show almost no guilt or remorse for any of their actions. I believe a psychopath is the one that has zero empathy.<br />Disclaimer: I just googled the above and have no expertise or qualifications on this topic. This is just a basic summary of a group of very complex mental disorders.<br /><br />I thought it was important to look at a rough definition of conduct disorder because we are included in all of John's innermost thoughts about death and how much delight he takes in thinking about the process of killing someone. He gives some quite vivid descriptions of his fantasies. That being said this was definitely YA fiction. Whilst there are some gruesome scenes the voice is distinctly adolescent. I know some people have drawn comparisons to the 'I Hunt Killers' series by Barry Lyga, but I think the John Cleaver series is a lot less sinister and dark. Seriously, I was traumatised by book 3 of 'I Hunt Killers.'<br /><br />I love stories where inherently 'bad' people struggle against their inner demons and this is a fine example of that. The very fact that John is in fact struggling with his urges and trying to suppress them shows us that he may not develop into a fully blown sociopath or psychopath. I liked the tension created by the author as John draws closer to the inevitable showdown between two twisted minds. I do think the lack of empathy thing was a bit laboured at points. I know this was being highlighted so we could really understand the inner turmoil he faced as he tried to stick to the rules he had set for himself to control his murderous urges, but there was a lot of repetition of this idea. I loved his coping strategy of saying nice things to people he wanted to hurt. It made for some lighter moments. <br /><br />Can John control his figurative inner demons in order kill the literal demon terrorizing his town with gruesome murders?<br /><br />A gritty thriller with a demonic twist.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1840023065666194686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_100439689" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/100439689" />
    <a title="Victoria Schwab" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1695365-victoria-schwab"><img alt="Victoria Schwab" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442505907p2/1695365.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/100439689?book_show_action=true">Apr 28, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Victoria Schwab" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Victoria Schwab" href="/user/show/1695365-victoria-schwab">Victoria Schwab</a>
      </span>

          added it

<div id="review_597618275" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597618275" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/597618275?book_show_action=true">Apr 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780755348817" href="/book/show/5981280-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer597618275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2453496667342371463">I'm going to stay nice and calm during this review. You know, calm. Ha. Ha. <br/><br/>OH MY GOSH. I AM SO FREAKED OUT RIGHT NOW. <br/><br/>But I will be calm. I promise. <br/><br/><b> If you're looking for a freaky YA book, this is it. </b> I'm not a YA horror expert, or anything, but this is the most scary book I've read. Which is why it got 5-stars, of course. Who doesn't like to be freaked out of their fuzzy socks?<br/><br/><b> Characters? </b> Our narrator is 15-year-old John Wayne Cleaver. He has sociopathic tendencies...so think of a person w</span>
  <span id="freeText2453496667342371463" style="display:none">I'm going to stay nice and calm during this review. You know, calm. Ha. Ha. <br><br>OH MY GOSH. I AM SO FREAKED OUT RIGHT NOW. <br><br>But I will be calm. I promise. <br><br><b> If you're looking for a freaky YA book, this is it. </b> I'm not a YA horror expert, or anything, but this is the most scary book I've read. Which is why it got 5-stars, of course. Who doesn't like to be freaked out of their fuzzy socks?<br><br><b> Characters? </b> Our narrator is 15-year-old John Wayne Cleaver. He has sociopathic tendencies...so think of a person who's devoid of empathy. I think he was written extremely well. He actually reminded me, a lot, of Christopher from The Curious Incident of the Dog in the Night-Time. Same style of voice. Same sort of intelligence and detachment from what humans categorise as "normal thinking". Basically, John freaked me out. <br><br>He wasn't just fighting murder, he was fighting tendencies. It says it in the blurb! <i> "He wants to be a good person, but fears he is a sociopath, and for years he has suppressed his dark side through a strict system of rules designed to mimic 'normal' behaviour." </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1381054664ra/4008246.gif" width="40" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>No, no! It's okay. I'm fine. I'll keep...writing this (without running around in ballistic circles checking under the bed and stuff).<br><br><b> There's so much talk about sociopaths and psychopaths and serial killers and mortuaries...I found the whole thing fascinating. </b> Not in the same way John did, though! Seriously. Noooo. It was fascinating in that I learnt how mortuaries embalm bodies, and how therapists talk to sociopaths and how parents struggle to relate to kids with no empathy. I really like seeing different angles in books, and this showed me a WHOLE new angle I'd never seen a book deal with. <br><br><b> My only complaint was that it's not realistic. </b> I thought it'd be a contemporary thriller. But it merges with paranormal. Maybe if you know that going in, it wouldn't be disappointing. But frankly, I like murder mysteries. I like the reality of find whodunnit. <br><br><b> Writing? </b> It's very factual. I've read <i> Partials </i> and <i> Fragments </i> by Dan Wells, and while I see a similarity in his styles, this is a whole other kettle of fish. While it's not gushing with emotional phrases, I enjoyed the detail and thought patterns. It's different. It tells it as it happens, with basically no empathy, but it's so horrible you're glued to the page. Instead of being emotionally involved. I'm emotionally scarred instead.<br><br><b> I'm also a fan of gallows humour. </b> John Green uses it. Doug McLeod uses it. The humour is dark and creepy and might "cross-the-line". Just don't take it too seriously. <br><br><b> I will never sleep again. </b> But hey. That's what freaky books are for.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1390904659ra/8297105.gif" width="40" height="100" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="2453496667342371463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1903779022" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1903779022" />
    <a title="Snotchocheez" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1899836-snotchocheez"><img alt="Snotchocheez" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1510561146p2/1899836.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1903779022?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snotchocheez" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snotchocheez" href="/user/show/1899836-snotchocheez">Snotchocheez</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1903779022" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1761814152237920822"><b>1.5 stars</b> <br/><br/>Despite the obvious similarity to Jeff Lindsay's <i> Dexter</i> series and the overwhelming feeling of revulsion from a YA-ish novel wallowing in the realm of real-life serial killers, I still was somewhat intrigued by Dan Wells' <b>I Am Not a Serial Killer</b> and plowed through the the first 100 pages like a starving man breaking a fast with an Italian BMT from Subway...<br/><br/>...but then realized that the delicious sandwich I'd been nom-noming on was made of inedible food stuff. (Wax? Offal? Fecal matte</span>
  <span id="freeText1761814152237920822" style="display:none"><b>1.5 stars</b> <br /><br />Despite the obvious similarity to Jeff Lindsay's <i> Dexter</i> series and the overwhelming feeling of revulsion from a YA-ish novel wallowing in the realm of real-life serial killers, I still was somewhat intrigued by Dan Wells' <b>I Am Not a Serial Killer</b> and plowed through the the first 100 pages like a starving man breaking a fast with an Italian BMT from Subway...<br /><br />...but then realized that the delicious sandwich I'd been nom-noming on was made of inedible food stuff. (Wax? Offal? Fecal matter?) <br /><br />Wells front-loads his thriller with umpteen references to the most notorious serial killers in history (everyone from Jack the Ripper to Ted Bundy to Ed Gein to Dennis Rader to Jeffrey Dahmer...hell, even the protagonist, 15 year-old John Wayne Cleaver {named for the famed actor} thinks he was <i> really</i> named after John Wayne <i> Gacy</i> the killer clown, and his father being named Sam Cleaver makes him the <i> Son Of Sam</i>...get it?) Yeah, our protag, young Mr. <i> Cleaver</i> (a mortuary owner's son in the tiny town of Conway...somewhere in the Midwest US) is obsessed with serial killers. Indeed, he's been diagnosed with sociopathic tendencies and Antisocial Personality Disorder, and is terribly concerned that the "monster inside" is trying to make him a serial killer, too. <br /><br />Then a real "serial killer" emerges, and begins terrorizing the residents of Conway, and the bodies start rolling into his mother's mortuary, and you just know Johnny's gonna lose his marbles over these gruesome murders and find the perpetrator, and<br />then<br />the<br />rug<br />is <br />pulled<br />out<br />from<br />under<br />the<br />reader.<br /><br />Everything from that point onward (roughly page 100 of 270) becomes laughable and utterly ridiculous. I should've known from the "Tor" imprint (of tor.com fame, the indie SF/fantasy publisher/website) that this was not going to be a conventional thriller, but the bait-and-switch (from straightforward serial killer story to a "supernatural thriller") was, for me, impossible to swallow. <br /><br />(Evidently not for others, though: there's at least three more "John Wayne Cleaver" sequels out there, with even higher GR star ratings than this one. Rest assured, though: I won't be torturing myself with them).</span>
  <a data-text-id="1761814152237920822" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_92187987" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92187987" />
    <a title="Annalisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa"><img alt="Annalisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1226336540p2/542037.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92187987?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Annalisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Annalisa" href="/user/show/542037-annalisa">Annalisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Trade Paperback 9780765327826" href="/book/show/7617119-i-am-not-a-serial-killer">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">dark psychology and crime thrillers without the grit</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Annalisa by: </span>
      Cami
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=guy-lit">guy-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=mystery-thriller">mystery-thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=voice">voice</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=character">character</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/542037-annalisa?shelf=psychology">psychology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92187987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2057204601048790042">John Wayne Cleaver knows he's a sociopath. He loves fire; he's curious about the insides of animals (and the dead bodies that come to mortuary owned by his mother); and he was a bed wetter. Anyone fascinated by serial killers (like John, okay and me) knows those are the three characteristics attributed to serial killers. In fear of his own dark potential, he follows rules to keep up the appearance of a normal teenager and keep himself safely away from danger. Then a serial killer strikes his tow</span>
  <span id="freeText2057204601048790042" style="display:none">John Wayne Cleaver knows he's a sociopath. He loves fire; he's curious about the insides of animals (and the dead bodies that come to mortuary owned by his mother); and he was a bed wetter. Anyone fascinated by serial killers (like John, okay and me) knows those are the three characteristics attributed to serial killers. In fear of his own dark potential, he follows rules to keep up the appearance of a normal teenager and keep himself safely away from danger. Then a serial killer strikes his town. In order to find and destroy the monster, John must let down his wall of rules and let his own monster out.<br /><br />Wells does such a good job putting you into John's head that you can root for him even while you're disturbed by him. He's a good kid, but I certainly wouldn't wish any girl to be his girlfriend or even his mom to be his mom. He made a fascinating protagonist as he struggled with his lack of empathy, how to read and connect with people, and where to find his moral ground. Wells asks the question of what makes a monster: the kid who restrains his dark tendencies, feeling nothing at the death he witnesses, or the one who kills out of need and cries for his victims. <br /><br />The plot took a disappointing turn, bringing in story elements that were unnecessary for the metaphorical message of John's battle (the only reason I didn't give it five stars), but the story was still fascinating and intense. It starts with an embalming and ends with, well I wouldn't tell you that. But it's good. If you are at all fascinated by sociopaths, serial killers, morticians, unconventional protagonists, or a little gore in your thrillers, than you'll enjoy this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2057204601048790042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
